## Instruction

I am a WooCommerce store owner, and my shop has warehouses in the following cities: New York, Boston, Dallas, LA, San Francisco, Houston. Please help me: Check each warehouse SQLite database (located in the warehouse directory in the workspace) for the latest product inventory list (identified by Product ID) that has been uploaded but not yet updated in the online WooCommerce store. Use the WooCommerce MCP server to synchronize the inventory updates to the WooCommerce online store according to the city-to-region mapping.

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import sqlite3
import os
import json

# Define the warehouse directory
warehouse_dir = "/workspace/dumps/workspace/warehouse"

# List of warehouse databases
warehouses = [
    "warehouse_new_york.db",
    "warehouse_boston.db",
    "warehouse_dallas.db",
    "warehouse_los_angeles.db",
    "warehouse_san_francisco.db",
    "warehouse_houston.db"
]

# City to region mapping
city_to_region = {
    "new_york": "East",
    "boston": "East",
    "dallas": "Central",
    "houston": "Central",
    "los_angeles": "West",
    "san_francisco": "West"
}

# Examine each warehouse database
warehouse_data = {}

for warehouse_file in warehouses:
    db_path = os.path.join(warehouse_dir, warehouse_file)
    city_name = warehouse_file.replace("warehouse_", "").replace(".db", "")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print(f"Examining: {warehouse_file}")
    print(f"City: {city_name.replace('_', ' ').title()}")
    print(f"Region: {city_to_region.get(city_name, 'Unknown')}")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    
    conn = sqlite3.connect(db_path)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    # Get table names
    cursor.execute("SELECT name FROM sqlite_master WHERE type='table';")
    tables = cursor.fetchall()
    print(f"Tables: {tables}")
    
    # Examine the structure and data
    for table in tables:
        table_name = table[0]
        print(f"\nTable: {table_name}")
        
        # Get table schema
        cursor.execute(f"PRAGMA table_info({table_name});")
        columns = cursor.fetchall()
        print(f"Columns: {[col[1] for col in columns]}")
        
        # Get all data
        cursor.execute(f"SELECT * FROM {table_name};")
        rows = cursor.fetchall()
        print(f"Number of rows: {len(rows)}")
        
        # Store data
        if city_name not in warehouse_data:
            warehouse_data[city_name] = {}
        
        warehouse_data[city_name][table_name] = {
            'columns': [col[1] for col in columns],
            'rows': rows
        }
        
        # Display first few rows
        if len(rows) > 0:
            print(f"\nFirst few rows:")
            for i, row in enumerate(rows[:5]):
                print(f"  {row}")
    
    conn.close()

print(f"\n{'='*60}")
print("Summary of warehouse data collected")
print(f"{'='*60}")
print(json.dumps({k: {table: len(v[table]['rows']) for table in v} for k, v in warehouse_data.items()}, indent=2))
 code
```

<div className="thinking-box">
üßê`Agent`

Perfect! I can see that each warehouse has:
- 17 products with inventory data
- All inventory records have `sync_status = 'pending'`, meaning they haven't been synchronized yet
- Products are identified by Product IDs (PROD001-PROD017)

Now let me check what products exist in the WooCommerce store and then synchronize the inventory. First, let me get all the pending inventory data from all warehouses:
</div>

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import sqlite3
import json

# Define the warehouse directory
warehouse_dir = "/workspace/dumps/workspace/warehouse"

# City to region mapping (correcting based on actual data)
city_to_region = {
    "new_york": "East",
    "boston": "East",
    "dallas": "Central",  # Database shows "South" but user said Central
    "houston": "Central",  # Database shows "South" but user said Central
    "los_angeles": "West",
    "san_francisco": "West"
}

# Warehouse files
warehouses = {
    "new_york": "warehouse_new_york.db",
    "boston": "warehouse_boston.db",
    "dallas": "warehouse_dallas.db",
    "los_angeles": "warehouse_los_angeles.db",
    "san_francisco": "warehouse_san_francisco.db",
    "houston": "warehouse_houston.db"
}

# Collect all pending inventory data
pending_inventory = {}

for city, db_file in warehouses.items():
    db_path = f"{warehouse_dir}/{db_file}"
    conn = sqlite3.connect(db_path)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    # Get pending inventory with product details
    query = """
    SELECT 
        i.product_id,
        p.product_name,
        p.category,
        p.price,
        p.description,
        i.quantity,
        i.last_updated,
        i.sync_status
    FROM inventory i
    JOIN products p ON i.product_id = p.product_id
    WHERE i.sync_status = 'pending'
    ORDER BY i.product_id
    """
    
    cursor.execute(query)
    rows = cursor.fetchall()
    
    region = city_to_region[city]
    
    for row in rows:
        product_id = row[0]
        if product_id not in pending_inventory:
            pending_inventory[product_id] = {
                'product_name': row[1],
                'category': row[2],
                'price': row[3],
                'description': row[4],
                'warehouses': {}
            }
        
        pending_inventory[product_id]['warehouses'][city] = {
            'quantity': row[5],
            'region': region,
            'last_updated': row[6],
            'sync_status': row[7]
        }
    
    conn.close()

# Display summary
print(f"Total unique products with pending inventory: {len(pending_inventory)}")
print("\nProduct Summary:")
print("="*80)

for product_id, data in sorted(pending_inventory.items()):
    print(f"\n{product_id}: {data['product_name']}")
    print(f"  Category: {data['category']}")
    print(f"  Price: ${data['price']}")
    print(f"  Warehouses with pending inventory:")
    
    # Group by region
    by_region = {}
    for city, wh_data in data['warehouses'].items():
        region = wh_data['region']
        if region not in by_region:
            by_region[region] = []
        by_region[region].append({
            'city': city,
            'quantity': wh_data['quantity']
        })
    
    for region in sorted(by_region.keys()):
        total_qty = sum(w['quantity'] for w in by_region[region])
        print(f"    {region}: {total_qty} units")
        for w in by_region[region]:
            print(f"      - {w['city'].replace('_', ' ').title()}: {w['quantity']}")

# Save to JSON for reference
output = {
    'summary': {
        'total_products': len(pending_inventory),
        'total_warehouses': len(warehouses),
        'city_to_region_mapping': city_to_region
    },
    'products': pending_inventory
}

with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/pending_inventory_summary.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(output, f, indent=2)

print("\n" + "="*80)
print("Summary saved to: pending_inventory_summary.json")
 code
```

<div className="thinking-box">
üßê`Agent`

Great! I can see there are many products in the WooCommerce store. Now let me create a comprehensive synchronization script that will:
1. Map warehouse inventory to WooCommerce products by SKU
2. Calculate regional inventory totals
3. Update regional products in WooCommerce
4. Mark inventory as synchronized in the databases
</div>

<div className="result-box">
<svg width="14px" height="14px" viewBox="0 0 32 32" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" style={{margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}}><path fillRule="evenodd" clipRule="evenodd" d="M13.0164 2C10.8193 2 9.03825 3.72453 9.03825 5.85185V8.51852H15.9235V9.25926H5.97814C3.78107 9.25926 2 10.9838 2 13.1111L2 18.8889C2 21.0162 3.78107 22.7407 5.97814 22.7407H8.27322V19.4815C8.27322 17.3542 10.0543 15.6296 12.2514 15.6296H19.5956C21.4547 15.6296 22.9617 14.1704 22.9617 12.3704V5.85185C22.9617 3.72453 21.1807 2 18.9836 2H13.0164ZM12.0984 6.74074C12.8589 6.74074 13.4754 6.14378 13.4754 5.40741C13.4754 4.67103 12.8589 4.07407 12.0984 4.07407C11.3378 4.07407 10.7213 4.67103 10.7213 5.40741C10.7213 6.14378 11.3378 6.74074 12.0984 6.74074Z" fill="#327EBD"/><path fillRule="evenodd" clipRule="evenodd" d="M18.9834 30C21.1805 30 22.9616 28.2755 22.9616 26.1482V23.4815L16.0763 23.4815L16.0763 22.7408L26.0217 22.7408C28.2188 22.7408 29.9998 21.0162 29.9998 18.8889V13.1111C29.9998 10.9838 28.2188 9.25928 26.0217 9.25928L23.7266 9.25928V12.5185C23.7266 14.6459 21.9455 16.3704 19.7485 16.3704L12.4042 16.3704C10.5451 16.3704 9.03809 17.8296 9.03809 19.6296L9.03809 26.1482C9.03809 28.2755 10.8192 30 13.0162 30H18.9834ZM19.9015 25.2593C19.1409 25.2593 18.5244 25.8562 18.5244 26.5926C18.5244 27.329 19.1409 27.9259 19.9015 27.9259C20.662 27.9259 21.2785 27.329 21.2785 26.5926C21.2785 25.8562 20.662 25.2593 19.9015 25.2593Z" fill="#FFDA4B"/></svg> `python-execute`

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import sqlite3
import json
from datetime import datetime

# Define the warehouse directory
warehouse_dir = "/workspace/dumps/workspace/warehouse"

# City to region mapping
city_to_region = {
    "new_york": "East",
    "boston": "East",
    "dallas": "Central",
    "houston": "Central",
    "los_angeles": "West",
    "san_francisco": "West"
}

# Warehouse files
warehouses = {
    "new_york": "warehouse_new_york.db",
    "boston": "warehouse_boston.db",
    "dallas": "warehouse_dallas.db",
    "los_angeles": "warehouse_los_angeles.db",
    "san_francisco": "warehouse_san_francisco.db",
    "houston": "warehouse_houston.db"
}

# Step 1: Collect pending inventory from all warehouses
print("="*80)
print("STEP 1: COLLECTING PENDING INVENTORY FROM WAREHOUSES")
print("="*80)

pending_inventory = {}
warehouse_inventory_ids = {}  # Track inventory IDs for later update

for city, db_file in warehouses.items():
    db_path = f"{warehouse_dir}/{db_file}"
    conn = sqlite3.connect(db_path)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    # Get pending inventory
    query = """
    SELECT 
        i.inventory_id,
        i.product_id,
        p.product_name,
        p.category,
        p.price,
        p.description,
        i.quantity,
        i.last_updated
    FROM inventory i
    JOIN products p ON i.product_id = p.product_id
    WHERE i.sync_status = 'pending'
    ORDER BY i.product_id
    """
    
    cursor.execute(query)
    rows = cursor.fetchall()
    
    region = city_to_region[city]
    
    print(f"\n{city.replace('_', ' ').title()}: {len(rows)} products pending sync")
    
    for row in rows:
        inventory_id = row[0]
        product_id = row[1]
        
        if product_id not in pending_inventory:
            pending_inventory[product_id] = {
                'product_name': row[2],
                'category': row[3],
                'price': row[4],
                'description': row[5],
                'regions': {}
            }
        
        if region not in pending_inventory[product_id]['regions']:
            pending_inventory[product_id]['regions'][region] = {
                'total_quantity': 0,
                'warehouses': {}
            }
        
        pending_inventory[product_id]['regions'][region]['warehouses'][city] = {
            'quantity': row[6],
            'last_updated': row[7]
        }
        pending_inventory[product_id]['regions'][region]['total_quantity'] += row[6]
        
        # Track inventory ID for update
        if city not in warehouse_inventory_ids:
            warehouse_inventory_ids[city] = []
        warehouse_inventory_ids[city].append({
            'inventory_id': inventory_id,
            'product_id': product_id
        })
    
    conn.close()

print(f"\n{'='*80}")
print(f"Total unique products to sync: {len(pending_inventory)}")
print(f"{'='*80}")

# Step 2: Prepare update data for WooCommerce
print("\n" + "="*80)
print("STEP 2: PREPARING WOOCOMMERCE UPDATE DATA")
print("="*80)

# Region name mapping for SKU prefix
region_sku_prefix = {
    "East": "EAST",
    "Central": "SOUTH",  # Note: Database uses "South" but we'll use "Central" for consistency
    "West": "WEST"
}

update_summary = {
    'products_by_region': {},
    'total_updates': 0
}

for product_id, product_data in sorted(pending_inventory.items()):
    print(f"\n{product_id}: {product_data['product_name']}")
    
    for region, region_data in product_data['regions'].items():
        total_qty = region_data['total_quantity']
        
        # Determine SKU prefix based on region
        sku_prefix = region_sku_prefix.get(region, region.upper())
        regional_sku = f"{sku_prefix}_{product_id}"
        
        print(f"  {region}: {total_qty} units (SKU: {regional_sku})")
        
        if region not in update_summary['products_by_region']:
            update_summary['products_by_region'][region] = []
        
        update_summary['products_by_region'][region].append({
            'product_id': product_id,
            'product_name': product_data['product_name'],
            'sku': regional_sku,
            'stock_quantity': total_qty,
            'warehouses': list(region_data['warehouses'].keys())
        })
        
        update_summary['total_updates'] += 1

# Save summary
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sync_plan.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(update_summary, f, indent=2)

print(f"\n{'='*80}")
print(f"Total regional products to update: {update_summary['total_updates']}")
print(f"Sync plan saved to: sync_plan.json")
print(f"{'='*80}")

# Display summary by region
print("\nSummary by Region:")
for region, products in update_summary['products_by_region'].items():
    print(f"\n{region}: {len(products)} products")
    for p in products[:3]:  # Show first 3
        print(f"  - {p['sku']}: {p['stock_quantity']} units")
    if len(products) > 3:
        print(f"  ... and {len(products) - 3} more")
 code
```

üßê`Agent`

Now let me create a Python script that will search for products by SKU in WooCommerce and update them with the new inventory quantities. I'll process this in batches to handle the API efficiently:
</div>

<div className="result-box">
<svg width="14px" height="14px" viewBox="0 0 32 32" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" style={{margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}}><path fillRule="evenodd" clipRule="evenodd" d="M13.0164 2C10.8193 2 9.03825 3.72453 9.03825 5.85185V8.51852H15.9235V9.25926H5.97814C3.78107 9.25926 2 10.9838 2 13.1111L2 18.8889C2 21.0162 3.78107 22.7407 5.97814 22.7407H8.27322V19.4815C8.27322 17.3542 10.0543 15.6296 12.2514 15.6296H19.5956C21.4547 15.6296 22.9617 14.1704 22.9617 12.3704V5.85185C22.9617 3.72453 21.1807 2 18.9836 2H13.0164ZM12.0984 6.74074C12.8589 6.74074 13.4754 6.14378 13.4754 5.40741C13.4754 4.67103 12.8589 4.07407 12.0984 4.07407C11.3378 4.07407 10.7213 4.67103 10.7213 5.40741C10.7213 6.14378 11.3378 6.74074 12.0984 6.74074Z" fill="#327EBD"/><path fillRule="evenodd" clipRule="evenodd" d="M18.9834 30C21.1805 30 22.9616 28.2755 22.9616 26.1482V23.4815L16.0763 23.4815L16.0763 22.7408L26.0217 22.7408C28.2188 22.7408 29.9998 21.0162 29.9998 18.8889V13.1111C29.9998 10.9838 28.2188 9.25928 26.0217 9.25928L23.7266 9.25928V12.5185C23.7266 14.6459 21.9455 16.3704 19.7485 16.3704L12.4042 16.3704C10.5451 16.3704 9.03809 17.8296 9.03809 19.6296L9.03809 26.1482C9.03809 28.2755 10.8192 30 13.0162 30H18.9834ZM19.9015 25.2593C19.1409 25.2593 18.5244 25.8562 18.5244 26.5926C18.5244 27.329 19.1409 27.9259 19.9015 27.9259C20.662 27.9259 21.2785 27.329 21.2785 26.5926C21.2785 25.8562 20.662 25.2593 19.9015 25.2593Z" fill="#FFDA4B"/></svg> `python-execute`

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import json

# Load the sync plan
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sync_plan.json', 'r') as f:
    sync_plan = json.load(f)

# Create a flat list of all products to update with their SKUs
products_to_update = []

for region, products in sync_plan['products_by_region'].items():
    for product in products:
        products_to_update.append({
            'region': region,
            'sku': product['sku'],
            'product_id': product['product_id'],
            'product_name': product['product_name'],
            'stock_quantity': product['stock_quantity'],
            'warehouses': product['warehouses']
        })

print(f"Total products to update: {len(products_to_update)}")
print("\nProducts to update:")
print("="*80)

for i, product in enumerate(products_to_update, 1):
    print(f"{i}. {product['sku']}: {product['stock_quantity']} units ({product['region']})")

# Save for next step
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/products_to_update.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(products_to_update, f, indent=2)

print("\n" + "="*80)
print("Products list saved to: products_to_update.json")
```

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import json

# Load products to update
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/products_to_update.json', 'r') as f:
    products_to_update = json.load(f)

# Create batches for WooCommerce API calls
# We'll search for products by SKU and prepare update data

print("="*80)
print("PREPARING WOOCOMMERCE PRODUCT UPDATES")
print("="*80)

# Group products by region for organized processing
products_by_region = {}
for product in products_to_update:
    region = product['region']
    if region not in products_by_region:
        products_by_region[region] = []
    products_by_region[region].append(product)

print(f"\nTotal products to update: {len(products_to_update)}")
print(f"Regions: {list(products_by_region.keys())}")

# Save SKU list for batch searching
sku_list = [p['sku'] for p in products_to_update]

with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sku_list.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(sku_list, f, indent=2)

print(f"\nSKU list saved for searching")
print(f"First 10 SKUs: {sku_list[:10]}")

# Create update plan
update_plan = {
    'total_products': len(products_to_update),
    'products_by_region': products_by_region,
    'all_skus': sku_list
}

with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/update_plan.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(update_plan, f, indent=2)

print("\nUpdate plan saved to: update_plan.json")
print("="*80)
 code
```

<Expandable title="Details">
```python

import json

# Since we need to call WooCommerce API from Python, let's create a mapping file
# that will help us identify which WooCommerce product IDs need to be updated

# Load the products to update
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/products_to_update.json', 'r') as f:
    products_to_update = json.load(f)

# Create a SKU to update data mapping
sku_to_update_data = {}
for product in products_to_update:
    sku_to_update_data[product['sku']] = {
        'stock_quantity': product['stock_quantity'],
        'region': product['region'],
        'product_id': product['product_id'],
        'product_name': product['product_name'],
        'warehouses': product['warehouses']
    }

# Save this mapping
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sku_to_update_mapping.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(sku_to_update_data, f, indent=2)

print("SKU to update data mapping created")
print(f"Total SKUs: {len(sku_to_update_data)}")
print("\nSample mappings:")
for i, (sku, data) in enumerate(list(sku_to_update_data.items())[:5]):
    print(f"  {sku}: {data['stock_quantity']} units")
 code
```

```json output_result
  EAST_PROD002: 1173 units
  EAST_PROD003: 1090 units
  EAST_PROD004: 891 units
  EAST_PROD005: 1116 units
=== EXECUTION INFO ===
```

```python

import json

# Load the WooCommerce products data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/hcqucjr9wZ55Z57xUCAy6Z.json', 'r') as f:
    wc_products_data = json.load(f)

# Parse the JSON content
wc_products = json.loads(wc_products_data['content'])

# Load our SKU mapping
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sku_to_update_mapping.json', 'r') as f:
    sku_mapping = json.load(f)

# Find matching products
matches = []
for product in wc_products:
    sku = product.get('sku', '')
    if sku in sku_mapping:
        matches.append({
            'wc_product_id': product['id'],
            'sku': sku,
            'current_stock': product.get('stock_quantity', 0),
            'new_stock': sku_mapping[sku]['stock_quantity'],
            'region': sku_mapping[sku]['region'],
            'product_name': product['name']
        })

print(f"Found {len(matches)} products to update in WooCommerce")
print("\nMatches found:")
print("="*80)

for match in matches[:10]:
    print(f"ID {match['wc_product_id']}: {match['sku']}")
    print(f"  Current: {match['current_stock']} ‚Üí New: {match['new_stock']}")
    print(f"  Region: {match['region']}")

if len(matches) > 10:
    print(f"\n... and {len(matches) - 10} more")

# Save matches for batch update
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/products_to_sync.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(matches, f, indent=2)

print("\n" + "="*80)
print(f"Total products matched: {len(matches)}")
print("Matches saved to: products_to_sync.json")
 code
```

```python

import json

# Load the WooCommerce products data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/hcqucjr9wZ55Z57xUCAy6Z.json', 'r') as f:
    wc_products_raw = json.load(f)

# The data structure contains the text content
wc_products = json.loads(wc_products_raw['text'])

# Load our SKU mapping
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sku_to_update_mapping.json', 'r') as f:
    sku_mapping = json.load(f)

# Find matching products
matches = []
for product in wc_products:
    sku = product.get('sku', '')
    if sku in sku_mapping:
        matches.append({
            'wc_product_id': product['id'],
            'sku': sku,
            'current_stock': product.get('stock_quantity', 0),
            'new_stock': sku_mapping[sku]['stock_quantity'],
            'region': sku_mapping[sku]['region'],
            'product_name': product['name']
        })

print(f"Found {len(matches)} products to update in WooCommerce")
print("\nMatches found:")
print("="*80)

for match in matches[:15]:
    print(f"ID {match['wc_product_id']}: {match['sku']}")
    print(f"  Current: {match['current_stock']} ‚Üí New: {match['new_stock']}")
    print(f"  Region: {match['region']}")

if len(matches) > 15:
    print(f"\n... and {len(matches) - 15} more")

# Save matches for batch update
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/products_to_sync.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(matches, f, indent=2)

print("\n" + "="*80)
print(f"Total products matched: {len(matches)}")
print("Matches saved to: products_to_sync.json")
 code
```

```json arguments
`*3

### Database Update After Sync
After successful WooCommerce update, mark inventory as synchronized in each warehouse database:
`*3sql
UPDATE inventory 
SET sync_status = 'synced', 
    sync_timestamp = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP 
WHERE sync_status = 'pending';
`*3
```
